Spot Price and Asset Classification in Hanafi Sales
Defining spot price and classifying assets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify physical assets in a sale as price or commodity using the Hanafi rule of the particle 'ba' and define 'thaman hal'.

Core Idea
In Hanafi sales, the particle 'ba' identifies the price; assets are classified as nuqud (always price), sila' (always commodity), or muqaddarat (ambiguous).

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains how to distinguish between price (thaman) and sold item (mabi') in Islamic sales. It categorizes physical assets into three types and gives a key grammatical rule: the particle 'ba' signifies the price. Understanding this classification is essential for determining the validity and payment terms of a sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three asset categories
Learn that physical assets (al-a'yan) are divided into nuqud (currencies), sila' (commodities), and muqaddarat (measured items). This classification determines their default role in a sale.
Nuqud are gold and silver coins (dinar/dirham).
2
Understand default roles
When non-currency items are sold for currency, the currency is the pure price (thaman mahd) and the other is the pure sold item (mabi' mahd).
This follows the nature of nuqud as athman.
3
Apply the grammatical rule
For ambiguous cases (e.g., two commodities exchanged), the particle 'ba' (with) in the contract indicates which item is the price – the item followed by 'ba' is the price, the other is the sold item.
Example: 'I sold this wheat with this cloth' – cloth is price.
4
Define spot price (thaman hal)
A spot price is a debt that has become due immediately, i.e., its term has ended (halla al-dayn). This is the opposite of a deferred price (mu'ajjal).
Thaman hal is payable at the time of contract.
5
Practice with a simple scenario
Given a sale of a cow for 10 dirhams, identify the price and the sold item. Then test with a barter: trade 5kg of rice for 10kg of wheat – which is price?
Use the 'ba' rule to decide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثمن حال . قوله: وبثمن؛ اعلم أن الأعيان ثلاثة: نقود، وسلع، ومقدرات، فبيع غير النقود بالنقود ويشتمل على المبيع المحض، والثمن المحض وماعدا ذلك يتردد بين كونه مبيعاً وثمناً، فالتمييز أن دخول الباء ثمن وغيره مبيع. قوله: حال؛ قال في المصباح المنير: حل الدين يحل بالكسر حلولاً: انتهى أجله فهو حال. انتهى. وفي منتهى الأرب واجب، ومنه الدين الحال: يعني خلاف مؤجل.
And with a spot price. His statement: and with a price; know that physical assets (al-a'yan) are of three types: currencies (nuqud), commodities (sila'), and measured items (muqaddarat). The sale of non-currencies for currencies includes the pure sold item and the pure price, and other than that vacillates between being a sold item and a price. So the distinction is that the particle 'ba' enters upon [that which is] the price, and the other is the sold item. His statement: spot (hal); he said in al-Misbah al-Munir: 'Halla al-dayn yahillu (with kasr) halulan: its term has ended, so it is spot (hal).' End. And in Muntaha al-Arab: 'obligatory,' and from it is al-dayn al-hal: meaning the opposite of deferred.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification ruling regarding the term 'thaman hal' (spot price) in sales. The commentator explains that physical assets in commerce fall into three categories: nuqud (currencies, mainly gold and silver), sil'a (commodities), and muqaddarat (measured items like weights and measures). When non-currency assets are sold for currency, the currency is the pure price and the non-currency is the pure sold item. In other cases, an asset may be ambiguous whether it functions as price or commodity. The rule is that the particle 'ba' (with) in the contract indicates which item is the price—the one preceded by 'ba' is the price, and the other is the sold item. Then 'hal' is defined as a debt whose term has become due and payable immediately, as opposed to a deferred debt (mu'ajjal). This classification is essential for determining the validity and conditions of a sale, especially regarding payment terms.

Key Terms
ثمن حال (thaman ḥāl): A price that is immediately due and payable at the time of the contract, not deferred.
نقود (nuqūd): Currencies, specifically gold and silver (dinar and dirham), which are always considered price (thaman) in sales.
سلع (sila‘): Commodities or goods that are sold, considered mabi' (sold item) when sold for currency.
مقدرات (muqaddarāt): Items that are measured or weighed, often considered mabi' when sold for currency, but can be price in certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the distinguishing feature that determines which item in a sale is the price?
A) The item of higher value is the price.
B) The item that is a currency is always the price.
C) The particle 'ba' enters upon the price, and the other is the sold item.
D) The seller's intention determines the classification.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales, the particle 'ba' in the contract designates the price, and assets are pre-classified into three categories to resolve ambiguity.

Defining Price and Commodity: The Role of the Particle 'Ba'
Defines thaman and mabi' using asset classification and the 'ba' rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between thaman and mabi' by applying the Hanafi rule of the particle 'ba' and classifying assets into nuqud, sila', and muqaddarat.

Core Idea
Whatever follows 'ba' in a sale contract is the price; everything else is the commodity.

In a sale contract, how do we know which item is the price and which is the commodity? The Hanafi school provides a clear linguistic rule: the particle 'ba' (meaning 'with') determines the price. This lesson unpacks that rule and the detailed categorization of assets that supports it, drawing from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah and Bada'i' al-Sana'i'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract formulation
Start with the actual wording of the sale, e.g., 'I sold you this item with that price'. The particle 'ba' appears before the item intended as the price.
The 'ba' is the key indicator; it is part of the classical contract phrase.
2
Classify the assets involved
Determine whether each asset is nuqud (dirhams/dinars), sila' (unique commodities), or muqaddarat (measured/weighed/counted items with equivalents). This classification affects the ruling.
Nuqud are always prices. Sila' are always commodities. Muqaddarat can be either depending on context.
3
Apply the 'ba' rule
If both assets are muqaddarat or one is muqaddarat and the other sila', the item following 'ba' is the price. If an asset is specified (mu'ayyan) vs. described (mawsuf), the rule still holds.
The rule is applied after classification; it resolves ambiguity.
4
Check special cases for fulus (copper coins)
Fulus are treated as prices when exchanged against a different genus or their own genus in equal number, but become commodities when exchanged against their own genus unequally.
This is an exception from the general rule.

Book of Sales / Valid Sales
And with a present price (Thaman Haal)
(With a present price)
[1] His statement: 'And with a price'; know that articles (a'yan) are three types: currencies (nuqud), commodities (sila'), and estimated goods (muqaddarat). The sale of non-currencies for currencies includes the pure commodity and the pure price. What is other than that fluctuates between being a commodity and a price. The distinction is that the entry of the letter 'ba' indicates the price, and the other is the commodity.
[2] His statement: 'present'; He said in al-Misbah al-Munir: 'The debt becomes due (yahillu) ... its term has ended, so it is present (haal).' End. And in Muntaha al-Arab: 'obligatory, and from it is a present debt,' meaning opposite of deferred.
(1) What the commentator defined as price and commodity is not absolute, and he will transmit in the chapter of Iqalah from Ibn Abidin the control of that, if Allah wills. The detail of that, as I mentioned in my memoranda in Fiqh of Transactions (p.117) from Bada'i' al-Sana'i' (5:233): First: Dirhams and dinars; they are prices in all cases because they are not specified by specification at all, so they are prices in all cases.
Second: What is other than dirhams and dinars from wealth; it has two states. The first: If it is something that has no similar (like unequal countable items and measured items), then it is a commodity in all cases because it becomes specified by specification; rather, its sale is not permissible except as a specified item, except described cloth sold on credit as salam, for it becomes a debt in the liability as a commodity through salam by istihsan contrary to qiyas due to people's need for salam in it. Likewise, the described item on credit in it not through salam becomes a debt in the liability as a price by istihsan. The second: If it is something that has a similar, like things measured by volume or weight or similar countable items, then it has two aspects:
1. If it is in exchange for a measured or weighed item for dirhams or dinars, it is a commodity.
2. If it is in exchange for a measured or weighed item for something that has no similar, then it has the following forms:
a. If the measured or weighed item is specified, it is a commodity.
b. If it is not specified, the letter 'ba' is judged; what it enters is the price, and the other is the commodity.
c. If one of them is specified and the other described, then the letter 'ba' is judged; what it accompanies is the price, and the other is the commodity.
d. If each of them is described, then the letter 'ba' is judged; what it accompanies is the price, and the other is the commodity.
Third: Current fulus (copper coins); if they are compared with a different genus, they are prices; likewise if compared with their own genus equal in number; and if compared with their own genus differing in number, they are a commodity.
(2) From al-Misbah al-Munir (p.47).
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling explaining how to distinguish between the price (thaman) and the commodity (mabi') in a sale contract. The author begins by stating that all articles (a'yan) fall into three categories: currencies (nuqud: dirhams and dinars), commodities (sila': goods that are not currencies and not measured/weighed), and estimated goods (muqaddarat: items sold by measure, weight, or count). When a non-currency is sold for a currency, the currency is clearly the price and the non-currency is the commodity. In other cases, the particle 'ba' (the preposition 'with' in the construction 'sold with X') determines which item is the price: whatever follows the 'ba' is the price, and the other is the commodity. The footnote from Bada'i' al-Sana'i' provides a detailed classification: dirhams and dinars are always prices because they are not specified by individual identification. Non-currency assets are either commodities in all cases (if they have no exact equivalent, like unique items) or they depend on context (if they have equivalents). For items with equivalents, the ruling varies based on what is exchanged and whether the items are specified or described. Finally, current coins (fulus) are prices when exchanged against a different genus or their own genus in equal number, but become commodities when exchanged against their own genus in unequal numbers. The key takeaway is that the Hanafi school uses the linguistic indicator of the 'ba' to determine the role of each item in the sale, ensuring clarity and preventing dispute.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale contract, identified as whatever follows the letter 'ba' in the contract formulation.
مبيع (mabi'): The commodity or object of sale, which is the item other than the price as determined by the 'ba'.
نقود (nuqud): Standard currency, specifically dirhams and dinars, which are always considered prices and cannot be specified individually.
سلع (sila'): Commodities that are not currencies and not measured/weighed goods; they are always commodities unless stated otherwise.
مقدرات (muqaddarat): Goods sold by measure, weight, or count that have equivalents; their status as price or commodity depends on the contract wording.
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as currency; their ruling as price or commodity depends on the exchange context as detailed in the passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of dirhams and dinars in all sales?
A) They are always commodities.
B) They are always prices (thaman).
C) They can be either depending on the contract wording.
D) They are never used as prices.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines price (thaman) and commodity (mabi') by the particle 'ba' in the contract and by classifying assets as nuqud, sila', or muqaddarat.

10 min
Sale with Absolute Price and Known Term
Explains ruling with proof: known term and absolute price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a known term in deferred sales and apply the Hanafi ruling when the price is absolute and currencies are equal in value and circulation.

Core Idea
When the price is absolute and currencies are equal, the buyer may choose any type — the seller's refusal is obstinacy.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains two interconnected rulings: the requirement that a deferred term be known to prevent dispute, and the buyer's freedom when the currency type is unspecified (thaman mutlaq) and currencies are equal. The commentary expands by considering circulation and presents four scenarios. Understanding these rulings empowers you to apply Hanafi fiqh to currency selection in sales, preventing obstinacy and ensuring fairness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage covers the condition of a known term in deferred sales and the ruling when the price is absolute (unspecified in description). Note that both relate to preventing dispute.
The text says 'And to a known term' then discusses absolute price.
2
Understand the condition for the term
The term (ajal) must be known because ignorance leads to dispute: the seller demands quick payment, the buyer delays.
This applies only when the sale is deferred and does not involve same genus + equal measure (riba al-nasa).
3
Analyze the absolute price
'Absolute' means the description (type) of currency is unspecified, not the amount. The commentary clarifies this to avoid misunderstanding.
The matn's wording might be ambiguous; the commentator resolves it.
4
Examine the four scenarios
The commentary lists four possibilities: equal value & circulation, differ in both, equal value only, equal circulation only. The first scenario is fully discussed.
Only the first scenario (equal in both) grants the buyer full choice.
5
Derive the ruling for the buyer's choice
When currencies are equal in monetary value and circulation, the buyer may pay any type he wishes. The seller cannot refuse, as refusal would be obstinacy (ta'annut).
If only one aspect is equal, the buyer must pay the superior one (more circulated or higher value).

وإلى أجل عُلِمَ. وبالثَّمَن المطلق ، فإن استوت ماليَّةُ النُّقُود، فعلى ما قُدِّرَ به من أي نوع شاء
[١] قوله : وإلى أجل ؛ يعني إذا بيعَ بخلاف جنسيه ولم يجمعهما قدر، فإنّه لو بيع مع جنسيه وجمعهما قدر لم يجز تأجيله لما فيه من ربا النَّساء كما صرح به غير واحدٍ من الفقهاء، ولعلَّ المصنف الله ترك هذا القيد اعتمادا على ما يأتي.
عُلِمَ ؛ إنما قيد الأجل بكونه معلوماً ؛ لأنَّ جهالة الأجل تفضي إلى المنازعة، فإنَّ البائع يطالب في مدة قريبة، والمشتري يأباها. [٢] قوله : أي لم يذكر ... الخ ؛ لما كان قول : المصنف له ؛ وهو المطلق موهماً أنّ المراد بالمطلق ما لم يذكر قدره ولا وصفه دفعه بأنَّ المراد : المطلق عن تسمية الوصف فقط.
[٣] قوله : فعلـى مـا قـدر به من أي نوع شاء ؛ من غير تقيد بنوع معين ؛ لأنه لا منازعة ؛ لاستوائها في الرّواج ، ولا اختلاف من الماليّة، وإن كان الاختلاف في الرواج فعلى ما هو أروج ، كذا صرحوا به فينبغي أن يقيد المصنّف له بهذا القيد. واعلم أنَّ المسألة رباعية، فإنَّ النقود
١. إما أن تستوي في المالية والرواج معاً.
٢. أو يختلف فيهما.
٣. أو تستوي في المالية فقط.
٤. أو الرواج فقط. ففي الصورة الأولى : المشتري بالخيارِ في دفع أيهما شاء، فلو طلب البائع أحدهما فللمشتري أن يدفع غيره ؛ لأنَّ امتناع البائع عن قبول ما دفعه المشتري تعنت ؛ لأنَّ الاختلاف في الاسم، ولا فضل لواحدٍ منهما على الآخر.
And to a known term. And with the absolute price, if the monetary value of the currencies is equal, then it is according to what was estimated from any type he wishes.
[1] His statement: 'And to a term.' It means if sold with a different genus and no equal measure, because if sold with its own genus and equal measure, its deferment is not permissible due to the presence of riba al-nasa as explicitly stated by more than one of the jurists. Perhaps the author (may Allah forgive him) omitted this condition relying on what will come.
'Known'; he only restricted the term to being known because ignorance of the term leads to dispute; the seller demands payment in a short period, and the buyer refuses it.
[2] His statement: 'He did not mention...' etc.; since the author's statement 'the absolute' might give the impression that by absolute is meant what does not mention its amount nor its description, he repels that by saying that what is meant is absolute from specifying the description only.
[3] His statement: 'Then according to what was estimated from any type he wishes' without restriction to a specific type, because there is no dispute due to their equal circulation and no difference in monetary value. If there is difference in circulation, then he pays the more circulated one. Thus they explicitly stated it, so the author should restrict it with this condition. Know that the issue has four scenarios: The currencies are 1. either equal in both monetary value and circulation, 2. or differ in both, 3. or equal in monetary value only, 4. or circulation only. In the first scenario: The buyer has the choice to pay whichever he wishes. If the seller demands one of them, the buyer may pay something else, because the seller's refusal to accept what the buyer pays is obstinacy, as the difference is only in name and there is no superiority of one over the other.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about two connected issues: the condition of a known term in deferred sales and the ruling when a sale is made with an absolute price (where the quality of the currency is unspecified). The author first clarifies that when a sale is made with a term (deferred payment), the term must be known to prevent dispute. He also notes that if the sale involves items of the same genus and equal measure, deferring payment is not permissible because of riba al-nasa (usury of delay). However, the author of the matn omitted this condition, possibly relying on later discussion. Then the commentary addresses 'absolute price': the phrase 'absolute' means that the type of currency is not specified (e.g., 'dirhams' without saying which kind). If the monetary value of all currency types is equal, the buyer may pay any type he wishes because there is no cause for dispute. The commentary further expands by considering circulation as well: if currencies differ in circulation, the buyer must pay the more circulated one. The issue is fourfold: (1) equal in both value and circulation: buyer chooses; (2) differ in both: the seller can demand the better? (not fully stated); (3) equal only in value: must pay the more circulated; (4) equal only in circulation: must pay the one of higher value? The text only elaborates on the first scenario where the buyer has full choice. The proof for these rulings is based on the principle of avoiding dispute and the prohibition of riba. The Hanafi position is practical: when there is no material difference, the buyer's freedom prevents the seller's obstinacy.

Key Terms
ثمن مطلق (thaman mutlaq): An absolute price where the type or quality of the currency is not specified in the sale contract.
أجل (ajal): The term or period for deferred payment in a sale; it must be known to avoid dispute.
ربا النساء (riba al-nasa): Usury of delay, which occurs when the exchange of two same-genus items is deferred without equal measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario where currencies are equal in both monetary value and circulation, who has the right to choose which currency to pay?
A) The seller
B) The buyer
C) Both must agree
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
When the price is absolute and currencies are equal in value and circulation, the buyer has the right to choose; the seller's refusal is obstinate.

Ruling on Sale with Thaman Mutlaq (Unspecified Currency)
Commentary on Al-Wiqayah's ruling for thaman mutlaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale with thaman mutlaq when currencies vary in value and circulation, and identify when the sale is sahih or fasid.

Core Idea
When the price is absolute, the buyer may pay any type if values and circulation are equal; otherwise, pay the more circulated currency, else the sale is invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a commentary on a matn from Al-Wiqayah concerning a sale where the price is mentioned without specifying the type of currency (e.g., 'ten dirhams'). The commentator outlines four scenarios based on the monetary value (maliyya) and market circulation (rawaj) of the currencies, and derives the ruling for each. The proof is rooted in the hadith on riba, which requires equality and spot exchange in certain items, analogically extended to currencies to prevent dispute and usury.

Guided Path
1
Define thaman mutlaq
Understand that thaman mutlaq means the price is expressed without describing the currency type, e.g., 'ten dirhams' without specifying silver or copper.
The commentator clarifies that 'absolute' here means free from description of the currency, not from the amount.
2
Identify the four scenarios
The commentator presents a four-fold classification: (1) equal value and circulation; (2) differ in both; (3) equal value only; (4) equal circulation only. For each, determine the ruling.
Memorize these four scenarios as they form the basis of the ruling.
3
Apply the ruling to each scenario
For scenario 1: buyer chooses any type. For 2 and 3: buyer must pay the more circulated currency. For 4: sale is invalid unless one type is specified.
The key is that in scenario 4, ignorance (jahalah) leads to dispute, so the sale is fasid.
4
Connect to the proof
The commentator cites the hadith on riba (silver for silver, etc.) to justify that currencies must be equal in value and exchanged hand-to-hand when specified; by analogy, when unspecified, the ruling ensures no riba or dispute.
This is a dalil naqli supported by qiyas.
5
Note the role of custom
The more circulated currency is determined by local custom (urf), which acts as a specification like text.
Custom (urf) is a recognized source in Hanafi fiqh for such determinations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلى أجل علم وبالثمن المطلق فإن استوت مالية النقود فعلى ما قدر به من أي نوع شاء [1] وإلى أجل علم. [2] وبالثمن (المطلق) : أي لم يذكر صفته بأن قيل : بعت بعشرة دراهم، (فإن استوت مالية النقود فعلى ما قدر به من أي نوع شاء) : أي يقع البيع على عشرة دراهم من أي نوع كان : أي يعطي المشتري أي نوع شاء [1] قوله : وإلى أجل ؛ يعني إذا بيع بخلاف جنسيه ولم يجمعهما قدر، فإنه لو بيع مع جنسيه وجمعهما قدر لم يجز تأجيله لما فيه من ربا النساء كما صرح به غير واحد من الفقهاء، ولعل المصنف ترك هذا القيد اعتمادا على ما يأتي. علم ؛ إنما قيد الأجل بكونه معلوماً ؛ لأن جهالة الأجل تفضي إلى المنازعة، فإن البائع يطالب في مدة قريبة، والمشتري يأباها. [2] قوله : أي لم يذكر ... الخ؛ لما كان قول المصنف له؛ وهو المطلق موهماً أن المراد بالمطلق ما لم يذكر قدره ولا وصفه دفعه بأن المراد : المطلق عن تسمية الوصف فقط. [3] قوله : فعلى ما قدر به من أي نوع شاء؛ من غير تقيد بنوع معين؛ لأنه لا منازعة؛ لاستوائها في الرواج، ولا اختلاف من المالية، وإن كان الاختلاف في الرواج فعلى ما هو أروج، كذا صرحوا به فينبغي أن يقيد المصنف بهذا القيد. واعلم أن المسألة رباعية، فإن النقود ١. إما أن تستوي في المالية والرواج معاً. ٢. أو يختلف فيهما. ٣. أو تستوي في المالية فقط. ٤. أو الرواج فقط. ففي الصورة الأولى : المشتري بالخيار في دفع أيهما شاء، فلو طلب البائع أحدهما فللمشتري أن يدفع غيره؛ لأن امتناع البائع عن قبول ما دفعه المشتري تعنت؛ لأن الاختلاف في الاسم، ولا فضل لواحد منهما على الآخر. (وإن اختلفت فعلى الأروج وفسد إن استوى رواجها إلا إذا بين أحدها) : أي في صورة اختلاف مالية النقود، إلا إذا بين أحدها) : أي أحد النقود، وهذا استثناء منقطع؛ لأن البحث في البيع بالثمن المطلق، فلا يكون حال بيان أحد النقود من جنس أحوال إطلاق الثمن، ثم بعد ذكر الثمن شرع في ذكر المبيع، فقال: (وفي الطعام والحبوب كيلا وجزافا إن بيع بغير جنسيه وفي الصورة الثانية : يصرف إلى الأروج تحرياً للجواز. وفي الصورة الثالثة أيضاً : يصرف إلى الأروج. وفي الصورة الرابعة : فسد البيع إلا أن يبين أحدهما؛ لأن الجهالة مفضية إلى المنازعة، إلا أن ترفع الجهالة. والبسط في «البحر» [1] قوله : فعلى الأروج؛ أي أروج النقود في البلد؛ إذ المتعارف بين الناس المعاملة بالنقد الغالب، فالتعيين بالعرف كالتعيين بالنص كما صرحوا به. [2] قوله : وفي الطعام؛ وهو الحنطة ودقيقها، وكذا سائر الحبوب كالعدس والحمص وغيرهما، وقال بعض المشايخ ما يقع في العرف على ما يمكن أكله من غير إدام كاللحم المطبوخ والمشوي ونحوه، قال صدر الشهيد : وعليه الفتوى. كذا في «مجمع الأنهر»، ولعل المصنف بهذا الوجه ذكر الحبوب بعد الطعام. [3] قوله : جزافاً؛ وهو البيع بالحدس والظن بلا كيل ووزن، ويجوز في جيمه الحركات الثلاث كما في «القاموس»، وهو معرب كزاف، وكزاف : بكسر أول بوزن خلاف بمعنى بهبوده هاشد بمعنى وبحساب ويحديهم آمده أسعت وبضم أول ميز هست. كذا في «البرهان القاطع». [4] قوله : إن بيع ... الخ؛ لقوله : «الزبيب بالزبيب، والفضة بالفضة، والبر بالبر، والشعير بالشعير، والتمر بالتمر، والملح بالملح، مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء، يداً بيد»
And to a known term. And with the absolute price. If the monetary value of currencies is equal, then upon what is estimated, from any type he wishes. [1] And to a known term. [2] And with the absolute price: i.e., he did not mention its description such that it was said: I sold for ten dirhams. (If the monetary value of currencies is equal, then upon what is estimated, from any type he wishes): i.e., the sale occurs for ten dirhams of any type: i.e., the buyer gives whichever type he wishes. [1] His statement: And to a term; means if he sold in a manner different from its two types and not combining them in quantity, then if he sold with its two types and combined them in quantity, it is not permissible to defer it due to what it contains of riba al-nasi'ah, as stated by more than one jurist. Perhaps the author left this condition relying on what follows. 'Known' – he only restricted the term to being known because ignorance of the term leads to dispute, for the seller demands at a short period and the buyer refuses. [2] His statement: i.e., he did not mention... etc.; since the author's statement 'absolute' might imply that 'absolute' means what is not mentioned in its amount nor its description, he repelled it by saying that 'absolute' means free from specifying the description only. [3] His statement: 'then upon what is estimated, from any type he wishes' – without restriction to a specific type; because there is no dispute due to equality in circulation and no difference in monetary value. If there is difference in circulation, then upon what is more circulated. Thus they explicitly stated, so the author should be restricted by this condition. Know that the issue is fourfold: currencies either (1) are equal in value and circulation together, (2) differ in both, (3) are equal only in value, (4) or only in circulation. In the first scenario: the buyer has the option to pay whichever he wishes; if the seller requests one of them, the buyer may pay other; because the seller's refusal to accept what the buyer pays is obstinacy, since the difference is in name and neither has superiority over the other. (And if they differ, then upon the more circulated, and it is invalid if their circulation is equal, unless he specifies one of them): i.e., in the scenario of difference in monetary value of currencies, unless he specifies one of them: i.e., one of the currencies. This is a disconnected exception because the discussion is about sale with the absolute price, so the case of specifying one of the currencies is not among the cases of absolute price. Then after mentioning the price, he began to mention the sold item, saying: (And regarding food and grains, by measure and by guess, if sold not with its two types. In the second scenario: it is directed to the more circulated seeking permissibility. In the third scenario also: it is directed to the more circulated. In the fourth scenario: the sale is invalid unless he specifies one of them, because ignorance leads to dispute, unless the ignorance is removed. The elaboration is in 'Al-Bahr'. [1] His statement: 'upon the more circulated'; i.e., the more circulated of currencies in the city; since the custom among people is dealing with the dominant currency, so specification by custom is like specification by text as they stated. [2] His statement: 'and regarding food'; it is wheat and its flour, and likewise other grains like lentils, chickpeas, and others. Some shaykhs said that which customarily falls under food is what can be eaten without relish, like cooked meat and roasted and the like. Sadr al-Shahid said: and the fatwa is upon it. So in 'Majma' al-Anhur'. Perhaps the author by this aspect mentioned grains after food. [3] His statement: 'by guess'; it is sale by estimation and conjecture without measure or weight. Its jim can have three vowels as in 'al-Qamus'. It is a Persian word [transliterated] meaning 'by guess' or 'by estimation'. As in 'al-Burhan al-Qati''. [4] His statement: 'if sold... etc.'; due to his saying: 'Raisins for raisins, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand.'
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the author's (likely from Al-Wiqayah) rulings on a sale where the price is stated in absolute terms (thaman mutlaq) without specifying the type of currency. The matn states: 'And to a known term. And with the absolute price. If the monetary value of currencies is equal, then upon what is estimated, from any type he wishes.' The commentator explains that 'absolute price' means the description of the currency is not mentioned, e.g., 'I sold for ten dirhams' without saying silver or copper. If the currencies have equal value (maliyya) and circulation (rawaj), the buyer may pay any type he chooses, and the seller cannot refuse. The commentator then outlines a four-fold classification: (1) currencies equal in both value and circulation – buyer's choice; (2) differ in both – the sale is directed to the more circulated to seek validity; (3) equal only in value – also directed to the more circulated; (4) equal only in circulation – the sale is invalid unless one type is specified, because ignorance leads to dispute. The commentator justifies this by citing the Hadith on riba: 'Raisins for raisins, silver for silver... like for like, hand to hand', implying that equality in value and spot exchange is required. He also notes that 'upon the more circulated' means the currency commonly used in the locality, as custom (urf) serves as specification like text. The passage also briefly touches on the sale of food and grains by measure or guess, where the same principles apply.

Key Terms
ثمن مطلق (thaman mutlaq): An unqualified price mentioned without specifying the type or description of currency, e.g., 'ten dirhams' without saying silver or copper.
نقود (nuqud): Currencies; specifically different types of dirhams (silver, copper, etc.) that may vary in value and circulation.
مالية (maliyya): Monetary value; the intrinsic worth or purchasing power of a currency.
رواج (rawaj): Circulation; the commonness and acceptability of a currency in the market.
جزاف (juzaf): Sale by guess or estimation without precise measure or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale for ten dirhams without specifying the type (thaman mutlaq), if the two currencies (e.g., silver and copper) have equal circulation but different values, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid and the buyer may pay whichever he wishes.
B) The sale is invalid unless the seller specifies one type.
C) The sale is valid only if the buyer pays the more circulated one.
D) The sale is invalid because the price is not known.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a sale with thaman mutlaq depends on the relationship between the value and circulation of the currencies; the more circulated currency prevails, and if circulation is equal but value differs, specification is required to avoid jahalah.

Ruling on Unspecified Currency in Sales
Explains the ruling when currency type is not specified in a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an unspecified price and explain how custom ('urf) functions as a specifying factor.

Core Idea
If the currency is not specified, the dominant custom sets the price; if ties, the sale is invalid.

This lesson examines a common transaction scenario: a sale where the price is stated but without specifying the currency type. The Hanafi jurists derived a nuanced ruling based on the principle that uncertainty leading to dispute invalidates the contract, but custom can resolve ambiguity. We will explore the four scenarios and the role of 'urf in clarifying the price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Understand that the discussion deals with a sale where the price is left absolute (thaman mutlaq) — no currency type is mentioned.
2
Map the four scenarios
Outline the four possible combinations: currencies differ in value (scenario 2/3), currencies equal in value (scenario 4), with or without specification of one currency.
The text presents these in brief; the commentary expands.
3
Apply the principle of jihalah
Recognize that uncertainty (jihalah) leading to dispute invalidates the sale. In scenario 4 (equal value, no specification), the uncertainty remains, so the sale is fasid.
Jihalah is a key invalidator in Hanafi contract law.
4
Analyze the role of custom ('urf)
Custom designates the dominant currency (al-arwaj) as the default price. The rule 'التعيين بالعرف كالتعيين بالنص' (specification by custom is like specification by text) applies.
This elevates 'urf to the level of a legal stipulation.
5
Understand the interrupted exception (istithna' munqati')
The exception 'except if one is specified' is munqati' because specifying a currency removes the absolute nature of the price, which is outside the original subject of discussion.
This usul point clarifies why the exception does not weaken the main rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع / البيوع الصحيحة
وإن اختلفت فعلى الأروج وفسد إن استوى رواجُها، إلا إذا بَيْنَ أَحَدَها.
[1] (وإن اختلفت فعلى الأروج وفسد إن استوى رواجها) : أي في صورة اختلاف ماليَّةِ النُّقُود، إلا إذا بَيْنَ أَحَدَها) : أي أحدَ النُّقُودِ، وهذا استثناء مُنْقَطِع ; لأنَّ البحث في البيع بالثَّمَنِ المطلق ، فلا يكون حال بيانٍ أحدِ النُّقُودِ من جنس أحوالِ إطلاقِ الثَّمَنِ.
وفي الصورة الثانية : يصرفُ إلى الأروج تحرياً للجواز.
وفي الصورة الثالثة أيضاً : يصرفُ إلى الأروج. وفي الصورة الرابعة : فسد البيع إلا أن يُبيّن أحدهما ; لأن الجهالة مفضية إلى المنازعة، إلا أن ترفع الجهالة.
قوله : فعلى الأروج ; أي أروج النقود في البلد ; إذ المتعارف بينَ النَّاسِ المعاملةُ بالنقد الغالب، فالتَّعيين بالعرف كالتَّعيين بالنص كما صرحوا به.
Book of Sales / Valid Sales. And if they differ, then (the price goes) to the most common, and it is invalid if their marketability is equal, except if one of them is specified. (1) (And if they differ, then to the most common, and it is invalid if their marketability is equal): i.e., in the case of difference in the value of currencies, except if one of the currencies is specified: i.e., one of the currencies, and this is an interrupted exception because the discussion is about sale with an absolute price, so the case of specifying one of the currencies is not of the same type as cases of absolute price. Then after mentioning the price, he began to mention the sold item, saying: (2) (And regarding food and grains by measure and by guess when sold with other than their genus. And in the second case: it is directed to the most common striving for validity. And in the third case also: it is directed to the most common. And in the fourth case: the sale is invalid unless one of them is specified, because ignorance leads to dispute, unless the ignorance is removed. And the elaboration is in 'al-Bahr'. He said: 'upon the most common': i.e., the most common currency in the country, since the customary practice among people is transacting with the dominant currency, so specification by custom is like specification by text as they have stated.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a sale is concluded without specifying which type of currency is intended as the price (thaman mutlaq). The author first states the rule: if the currencies have different market values, the price is understood to be the most common (arwaj) currency in the country; if they have equal value, the sale is invalid unless the buyer or seller specifies one. The commentator clarifies that the exception (specifying one currency) is an interrupted exception (istithna' munqati') because specifying a particular currency removes the ambiguity inherent in an absolute price. Four scenarios are outlined: if the currencies differ in value, the price defaults to the most common; if they are equal in value, the sale is invalid unless one is specified; if one is specified, the sale is valid; if none is specified and they are equal, the sale is invalid due to uncertainty leading to dispute. The commentary further notes that custom ('urf) serves as a means of specification, akin to explicit textual stipulation, and therefore the dominant currency becomes the default.

Key Terms
الأروج (al-arwaj): The most common currency in circulation in a given locality.
استثناء منقطع (istithna' munqati'): An interrupted exception where the excepted item is not of the same category as the general case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale where the price is left unspecified and there are two currencies of equal market value, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The sale is valid and the price is split equally.
B) The sale is invalid unless one currency is specified.
C) The sale is valid and the buyer may choose which currency to pay.
D) The sale is invalid and cannot be rectified.

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) functions as a specifying factor in ambiguous sales, and uncertainty leading to dispute invalidates the contract.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

General Rule for Selling Food by Guess Against a Different Genus
Definitions and general ruling with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for selling foodstuffs by guess (juzafan) when the species differs, and apply the hadith to determine validity.

Core Idea
Selling food by guess against a different species is valid hand-to-hand, but invalid against the same species except for a small amount.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational rule for selling foodstuffs when the price is paid in a different kind. The commentator defines key terms and cites the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit, which permits such sales only if they are hand-to-hand. We will also see an exception for very small quantities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text deals with selling food (ta'am) or grains by guess (juzafan) when the price is of a different species. The general ruling is that it is valid, provided the sale is hand-to-hand (spot).
The definition of 'food' includes wheat, flour, grains, and customarily eaten items without condiment.
2
Cite the dalil
The hadith of Ubadah is quoted: when species differ, you may sell as you wish, but hand-to-hand. This is the primary evidence for the permissibility.
The hadith is narrated by all except al-Bukhari; it is ahad in transmission (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalalah).
3
Apply the exception
If the sale is against the same species and by guess, it is invalid due to riba, unless the quantity is very small (less than half a sa'), because there is no legal standard for such a small amount.
Half a sa' is the minimum standard (mithqal shar'i) for measurement in such cases.
4
Define juzaf
Juzafan means sale by estimation, without exact measurement. The term is a Persian loanword and is permissible when the species differ.
The three vowel movements on the jim are all allowed.

Source Text

وفي الطعام والحبوب كَيْلاً وَجُزَافًا إِنْ بِيعَ بِغَيْرِ جنسيه
[2] ( وفي الطعام والحبوب كَيْلاً وجُزَافًا إِنْ بِيعَ بِغَيْرِ جنسيه ) 
قوله : وفي الطعام ; وهو الحنطة ودقيقها، وكذا سائر الحبوب كالعدس والحمص وغيرهما، وقال بعض المشايخ ما يقعُ في العرف على ما يمكن أكله من غير إدام كاللحم المطبوخ والمشوي ونحوه، قال صدر الشهيد : وعليه الفتوى. كذا في «مجمع الأنهر) ، ولعل المصنّف له بهذا الوجه ذكر الحبوب بعد الطعام. 
قوله : جُزافاً ; وهو البيع بالحدس والظن بلا كيل ووزن، ويجوز في جيمه الحركات الثلاث كما في «القاموس، وهو معرب كزاف، وكزاف : بكسر أول بروزن خلاف بمعنی بهبوده هاشد بمعنى وبحساب ويحديهم آمده أسعت وبضم اول ميز هست. كذا في «البرهان القاطع». 
قوله : إن بيع ... الخ ; لقوله : «الزبيب بالزبيب، والفضة بالفضة، والبر بالبر، والشعير بالشعير، والتمر بالتمر، والملح بالملح ، مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء، يداً بيد، فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم ، إذا كان يدا بيد» رواه الجماعة إلا البخاري من حديث عبادة بن الصامت له ، بخلاف ما إذا بيع بجنسه مجازفة، فإنّه لا يصح; لاحتمال الرّبا إلا إذا كان قليلاً، وهو ما دون نصف الصاع ; لعدم العيار الشرعي، وهو نصف صاع كذا صرحوا به.
وبإناءٍ وحَجَرٍ مُعين لم يُدْرَ قدره، وفي صاع في بيع صُبْرَةٍ كُلٌّ صَاعِ بِكَذَا) : أي إذا قال : يُعْتُ هذه الصُّبْرَة كُلُّ صَاعِ بدرهم صح في صاع واحد" ، وفي كلها إِنْ سَمَّى جُملةً قفزانِها ) : أي إذا قال: يعْتُ هذه الصُّبْرَة ، وهي عشرةُ أَقْفِزَة، كُلُّ قفيز بدرهم صح في الكل، وفسد في الكل في بيد، 
[١]قوله : وبإناء... الخ ; لأنّ هذه الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة ; لأنَّ البيع يوجبُ التسليم في الحال، وهلاكه قبل التسليم نادر.
[٢] قوله : لم يدر قدره ; إذا لم يحتمل الإناء النقصان، والحجر التفتت، كأن يكون من خشب أو حديد، فإنّ احتمالهما لم يجز كما صرحوا به.
[٣] قوله : صح في صاع واحد ; عند الإمام الله له ، وفي الكل عند صاحبيه، وهو قول الشافعي ومالك وأحمد الله ; لأن المبيع معلوم بالإشارة، فلا يحتاج إلى معرفة مقداره ، وما فيه من الجهالة لا يضرّ ; لأن رفعه بيدهما ، بأن يكيلا الصبرة في المجلس. ولأبي حنيفة له : إن الثَّمن مجهول ; لأنَّ جملة الأفراد غير معلومة، فيكون ما بإزائها من الثَّمن مجهولاً ، إلا أنَّ الأقل وهو الواحد معلوم ، فيصح البيع ويفسد فيما عداه إلا أن ترتفع الجهالة بتسمية جميع الأفراد أو بالكيل في المجلس. [٤] قوله : فسد ... الخ ; ; لأنه ينصرفُ إلى الواحد والواحدة منها متفاوتة، فلا يصح البيع في واحد منها ، بخلاف مسألة الصبرة.
And regarding food and grains by measure and by guess when sold with other than their genus. (2) (And regarding food and grains by measure and by guess when sold with other than their genus). He said: 'and regarding food': it is wheat and its flour, and likewise other grains such as lentils, chickpeas, and others. Some scholars said that what is customarily considered as something eaten without a condiment, like cooked meat, roasted meat, etc. Sadr al-Shahid said: and the fatwa is upon it. Likewise in 'Majma' al-Anhar'. Perhaps the author mentioned grains after food for this reason. He said: 'by guess' (juzafan): it is a sale by estimation and conjecture without measure or weight. Its jim may take the three vowel movements as in 'al-Qamus'. It is a Persian loanword: kazaf, and kazaf: with kasra on the first, weight of khilaf, meaning 'improvement' (?) ... He said: 'when sold' etc., due to his saying: 'Raisins for raisins, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand, and if these types differ, then sell as you wish, provided it is hand to hand' narrated by the group except al-Bukhari from the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit, may Allah be pleased with him. Contrary to when it is sold with its own genus by guess, then it is not valid due to the possibility of riba unless it is a small amount, which is less than half a sa', because there is no legal standard, which is half a sa', as they have stated. And [the sale] with a known container and a known stone whose capacity is unknown, and with a sa' in the sale of a pile: 'each sa' for such amount', i.e., if he says: I sold this pile, each sa' for a dirham, it is valid for one sa'. And in all of them if he specifies the total number of qafiz: i.e., if he says: I sold this pile, which is ten qafiz, each qafiz for a dirham, it is valid for all. And it is invalid in all in [another case]... (1) He said: 'and with a container' etc., because this ignorance does not lead to dispute because the sale requires immediate delivery, and its destruction before delivery is rare. (2) He said: 'its capacity is unknown' if the container cannot be reduced and the stone cannot be crushed, like if made of wood or iron, but if they can be, it is not permissible as they have stated. (3) He said: 'valid for one sa' according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) Allah, and for all according to his two companions, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, because the sold item is known by indication, so there is no need to know its amount, and the ignorance in it is not harmful because its removal is in their hands, i.e., they can measure the pile in the session. According to Abu Hanifa, the price is unknown because the total of the individuals is unknown, so what corresponds to it from the price is unknown, except that the minimum, which is one, is known, so the sale is valid and invalid for the rest unless the ignorance is removed by specifying all individuals or by measuring in the session. (4) He said: 'invalid' etc., because it refers to the one, and the individual (sa') are unequal, so the sale is not valid in any one of them, contrary to the case of the pile.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage deals with the rules for selling foodstuffs and grains when the price is paid in a different species (i.e., not in the same kind). The commentator first defines 'food' (ta'am) broadly as wheat and its flour, and all grains like lentils and chickpeas. Some scholars extend it to anything customarily eaten without a condiment, such as cooked meat. The term 'juzafan' means selling by guess, without exact measurement; it is a Persian loanword. The hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit is cited to establish the prohibition of riba when selling similar items by weight or measure; if the species differ, sale is allowed hand-to-hand. However, if sold by guess against the same species, it is invalid except in a small quantity (less than half a sa') because there is no precise standard. The text then addresses specific cases: selling with a known container whose capacity is unknown - this is permissible because the ignorance does not lead to dispute, as the sale requires immediate delivery. If the container or stone cannot be reduced (e.g., made of iron), the ignorance is acceptable; if it can be reduced, it is not allowed. The next case is selling a pile (subrah) where the seller says 'each sa' for a dirham.' Here, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only one sa' is validly sold because the total number is unknown, making the price unknown; but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider the sale valid for the entire pile because the pile is known by indication and the parties can measure it in the session. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools agree with the disciples. However, if the seller specifies the total quantity (e.g., 'this pile is ten qafiz, each qafiz for a dirham'), the sale is valid for all. Finally, if the pile consists of unequal individual units (e.g., different sized containers), the sale is invalid because each unit is different and the price cannot be allocated.

Key Terms
جزافا (juzafan): Selling by estimation or guess without precise measurement (weight or volume).
صاع (sa'): A unit of volume approximately 2.5-3 kg for grains. Half a sa' is the minimum standard for measurement in rulings of riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, what condition is required when selling food by guess against a different species?
A) The food must be precisely measured.
B) The sale must be hand-to-hand (spot).
C) The price must be paid in the same species.
D) The quantity must be less than half a sa'.

Key Takeaway
Selling food by guess against a different species is valid only if the sale is spot (hand-to-hand).

The Subrah Dispute: Selling a Pile by Per-Unit Price
Intra-Hanafi dispute on subrah sale with proof and practical consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's position and that of his two disciples regarding the sale of a pile (subrah) when the price per unit is stated but total quantity is unknown, and evaluate the practical consequence.

Core Idea
When selling a pile by 'each sa' for a dirham', Abu Hanifa validates only one sa'; the disciples validate the whole pile — the difference turns on whether ignorance of total price is harmful.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: a seller says 'I sell you this pile (subrah), each sa' for a dirham' without specifying the total number of sa's. Imam Abu Hanifa considers the total price unknown, so only one sa' is validly sold. His disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with the other three Sunni schools, hold the entire sale valid because the pile is known by indication and ignorance can be removed later. We will analyze both proofs and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Define the subrah transaction
A subrah is a pile of grain that is not measured. The seller says 'each sa' (unit) for a dirham,' without stating how many sa's are in the pile. The buyer agrees.
This is a common transaction in traditional markets.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the sale is valid only for one sa' because the total quantity of the pile is unknown, making the total price (number of sa's × 1 dirham) unknown. The minimum known is one sa', so only that is valid.
He considers the ignorance (jihalah) in the price harmful because it cannot be cured after the contract.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the sale is valid for the entire pile. Their evidence: the sold item (the pile) is known by physical indication (isharah), so its precise amount need not be known. Any ignorance is removable by measuring the pile during the session.
This view is also held by al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
If the buyer takes the pile without measuring, according to Abu Hanifa only one sa' is sold, and the rest is not. According to the Sahibayn, the entire pile is sold for the total price based on the number of sa'.
If they measure later, according to Abu Hanifa the ignorance is removed and the sale becomes valid for the whole.
5
Note the exception when total is specified
If the seller says 'This pile is ten sa', each sa' for a dirham,' then the sale is valid for all according to all Hanafi authorities because the total price is known.
Similarly, if they measure in the session, the sale becomes valid for the whole.

Source Text

The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools agree with the disciples. However, if the seller specifies the total quantity (e.g., 'this pile is ten qafiz, each qafiz for a dirham'), the sale is valid for all. Finally, if the pile consists of unequal individual units (e.g., different sized containers), the sale is invalid because each unit is different and the price cannot be allocated.

Key Terms
صبرة (subrah): A pile of grain or foodstuff that is not measured or weighed.
إشارة (isharah): Pointing or indication; the sold item is known by physically pointing to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a seller says 'I sell you this pile of dates, each sa' for one dirham,' without specifying the total number, how many sa' are validly sold?
A) The entire pile.
B) Only one sa'.
C) None, because the price is unknown.
D) Only if the buyer measures immediately.

Key Takeaway
The subrah dispute shows that within the Hanafi school, the same transaction can be ruled valid or limited based on how we evaluate ignorance (jihalah).

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Selling a Heap per Unit: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling a heap by measure per unit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on selling a heap (subrah) per unit and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and the two disciples' (Sahibayn) views on the validity of such a sale.

Core Idea
Selling a heap 'each sa' for a dirham' is valid only for one unit according to Abu Hanifa, but valid for all according to the Sahibayn, because ignorance (jahalah) can be removed by measuring.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya deals with a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on selling a heap of grain per unit without specifying the total. The central question is whether the ignorance of total quantity (jahalah) renders the sale invalid. Abu Hanifa restricts validity to one unit, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, uphold the entire sale as valid, a position also held by the other Sunni schools. The dispute hinges on whether jahalah leads to dispute and whether it can be removed during the contract session.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The sale of a heap (subrah) of grain where the seller says 'each sa' for one dirham' without specifying the total number of sa'. Determine whether the sale is valid, invalid, or partially valid.
This is the core scenario.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that only one sa' is validly sold; the rest of the heap remains unsold because the total price is unknown. His proof: jahalah in the total price leads to dispute, invalidating the sale of the remainder.
He argues that the price for the additional units is unknown.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the entire sale is valid. Their proof: the sold item is known by indication (isharah), and the jahalah can be removed by measuring the heap in the session, so it does not lead to dispute.
They also cite that the buyer has the option to measure.
4
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
Imam al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad agree with the Sahibayn, making this a case where the Hanafi majority aligns with the other schools against Abu Hanifa's individual view.
The disagreement is only within the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, under Abu Hanifa's view, the seller must either specify the total or measure the heap in the session for the sale to be fully valid. Under the Sahibayn's view, the sale is initially valid for all, and the buyer can later measure to remove ignorance.
This affects contract drafting and dispute resolution.

And with a container and a specific stone whose quantity is not known, and with a sa' in selling a heap (subrah): every sa' for such and such. And in all of it if he specified the total number of qafiz, and it is invalid in all in selling a flock (thullah) or cloth, every sheep or cubit for such and such. And likewise every countable (item) that varies. Then if he sold a heap on the basis that it is one hundred sa' for one hundred (dirhams), and it is less or more, the buyer takes the lesser with its proportion, or he cancels the sale, and what is extra is for the seller. His statement: 'And with a container...' etc. Because this ignorance does not lead to dispute; because the sale necessitates immediate delivery, and its destruction before delivery is rare. His statement: 'did not know its quantity' – when the container does not admit of decrease and the stone of crumbling, like if it is of wood or iron, for if they admit of (decrease/crumbling) it is not permissible as they explicitly stated. His statement: 'valid in one sa'' – according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) – may Allah have mercy on him – and valid in all according to his two companions, and it is the statement of al-Shafi'i, Malik and Ahmad – may Allah have mercy on them – because the sold item is known by indication, so there is no need to know its quantity, and the ignorance (jahalah) in it does not harm because its removal is in their hands, by them measuring the heap in the session. And for Abu Hanifa – may Allah have mercy on him – indeed the price is unknown because the total number of units is unknown, so what is in exchange for it of the price is unknown, except that the least, which is one, is known, so the sale is valid and invalid in what is beyond it unless the ignorance is removed by specifying all the units or by measuring in the session. His statement: 'invalid...' etc. Because it refers to the individual one and they vary, so the sale of one of them is not valid, unlike the issue of the heap. His statement: 'thullah' – with fatha, meaning a large flock of sheep and goats mixed or specifically sheep. 'Thull' plural, like 'unub', and 'thilal' plural, like 'kitab'. His statement: 'and likewise' – i.e., likewise the sale is invalid in all in selling every countable item that varies; because it cannot be directed to all due to ignorance of the sold and the price, nor to one because it varies, and that leads to dispute, unlike the first. And according to them (the two companions): it is valid in all. And the dispute is when he did not specify the total price nor the total of the flock; but if he specified the total price and the total of the flock, or specified the total of the flock and did not specify the total price, then it is permissible by agreement. Thus mentioned al-Birjandi quoting from al-Mujtaba. His statement: 'the buyer takes the lesser with its proportion' – if he wishes, because the measure is part and the measure is divisible into parts, or he cancels if he wishes, because when the expense was distributed over him his satisfaction with what exists is not complete. And with this Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad – may Allah have mercy on them – say. And in Fatawa Qadi Khan: Indeed the option is when he has not received the sold item or has received some but not others; but if he received all then there is no option for him, rather he takes by proportion. His statement: 'the extra is for the seller' – because it remains his property; because the sale occurred on a specific quantity, and what occurs on a specific quantity does not encompass other than it.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about selling a heap (subrah) or similar undefined quantities per unit. It opens with a general principle: selling a known container or stone without knowing its exact volume is permissible because the ignorance (jahalah) does not lead to dispute, as the contract requires immediate delivery and destruction before delivery is rare. The main issue: if someone sells a heap of grain saying 'each sa' for one dirham', Abu Hanifa rules that the sale is valid only for one sa' (the minimum) and invalid for the rest, because the total price is unknown. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that the sale is valid for the entire heap, because the subject matter is known by indication and the ignorance can be removed by measuring in the session. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools agree with the two disciples. However, if the seller specifies the total number of qafiz (e.g., 'this heap of ten qafiz, each qafiz for one dirham'), then the sale is valid for all by agreement. The same dispute applies to selling a flock of sheep or a roll of cloth per unit. If the items are individually variable (like different sheep or cubits), the sale is invalid altogether because even one unit is unknown and variable. The passage also discusses a case where a heap is sold on the assumption it contains a certain measure but it turns out less or more: the buyer has the option to take the actual amount at the proportional price or cancel the sale; any excess remains the seller's property. This ruling is agreed upon. Key terms: 'subrah' (heap of unmeasured grain), 'thullah' (flock), 'jahalah' (ignorance leading to dispute). The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as the dispute between Imam and his disciples is well-known.

Key Terms
صُبْرَة (subrah): A heap of grain or food without measurement or weight, sold in bulk.
ثلة (thullah): A flock of sheep, specifically a large number or of sheep only (as per Qamus).
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance about the quantity or quality of the subject matter or price that could lead to dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when someone sells a heap of grain saying 'each sa' for one dirham' without specifying the total, how many sa' are validly sold?
A) All the sa' in the heap
B) Only one sa'
C) None, the sale is entirely invalid
D) The sale is valid only if the buyer measures it in the session

Key Takeaway
The validity of a 'per unit' sale of an unmeasured heap depends on whether jahalah can be easily removed; Abu Hanifa restricts it to one unit, while his disciples and later practice allow it for all units with an option to measure.

Rulings on Selling Variable Units: Flocks, Piles, and Cloth
Explains rulings for sales of differing units and quantities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sales of variable units (flock per head, pile of grain, cloth per cubit) and apply the distinction between description (wasf) and essence (asl) to determine who gets the surplus.

Core Idea
Uncertainty invalidates sales of variable units unless totals are specified; the classification of the unit determines the allocation of surplus.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh commentary addresses three common sales where the unit of sale varies: selling a flock of sheep by the head, selling a pile of grain based on a claimed quantity, and selling cloth by the cubit. The rulings hinge on two key factors: whether the total price and quantity are specified, and whether the unit is considered a description (wasf) or an essence (asl). Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining the rights of buyer and seller when actual quantities differ from stated ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sales and their common issue
List the three cases: flock per head (each sheep), pile of grain (claimed measure), cloth per cubit. Note that all involve a variable unit that could lead to uncertainty (jahalah) if totals are not specified.
The common thread is that the sale is per unit of a divisible item, but the unit itself may not be uniform.
2
Determine the condition for validity in each case
For the flock, the sale is fasid unless the total price and total quantity are specified. For the pile, the buyer gets an option if the actual differs from the claimed. For cloth, the cubit is a description, so surplus goes to the buyer without the seller's option.
The condition for validity in the flock case is a point of divergence between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples.
3
Analyze the buyer's options when actual quantity differs
In the pile sale, the buyer may take the actual amount for its share of the price or cancel. In the cloth sale, the buyer takes the extra length without any option for the seller.
The key distinction is that the measure in the pile is an essence (asl), while the cubit in cloth is a description (wasf).
4
Understand the wasf vs asl distinction
A description (wasf) is an attribute that affects the value of the item when present or absent, like length in cloth. An essence (asl) is the substance itself, like the quantity of grain. Surplus of a description goes to the buyer; surplus of an essence goes to the seller.
This distinction is defended by the commentator with multiple rational arguments: things damaged by reduction have description, etc.
5
Apply the distinction to new cases
Given a new scenario, classify the unit as description or essence based on whether its increase or decrease affects the value of the remaining item. Then determine who gets the surplus.
For example, wool sold by weight: weight is essence, so surplus goes to seller. A carpet sold by length: length is description, so surplus goes to buyer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع/ البيوع الصحيحة
ثلة أو ثوب، كل شاة أو ذراع بكذا، وكذا كل معدود متفاوت. فإن باع صبرة على أنها مائة صاع بمئة، وهي أقل أو أكثر أخذ المشتري الأقل بحصته، أو فسخ البيع، وما زاد للبائع.
(1) قوله: ثلة؛ بالفتح رمه بزرك آن كوسفند و بزور آمیخته یا خاص ست برمه ميش ثلل كعنب وثلال ككتاب جمع . كذا في منتهى الآرب، وفي القاموس: جماعة الغنم، والكثير منها، أو من الضأن خاصة.
(2) قوله: وكذا؛ أي وكذا فسد البيع في الكل في بيع كل معدود متفاوت؛ لأنه لا يمكن الصرف إلى الكل؛ لجهالة المبيع والثمن، ولا إلى واحد؛ لأنه متفاوت، فيفضي إلى المنازعة بخلاف الأولى، وعندهما: يجوز في الكل. والخلاف فيما إذا لم يبين جملة الثمن، ولا جملة القطيع، فإن بين جملة الثمن وبين جملة القطيع، أو بين جملة القطيع ولم يبين جملة الثمن فيجوز اتفاقاً. كذا ذكره البرجندي نقلا عن المجتبى.
(3) قوله: أخذ المشتري الأقل بحصته؛ إن شاء لأن الكيل جزء، والكيل ينقسم على الأجزاء، أو فسخ إن شاء؛ لأن النفقة لما تفرقت عليه لم يتم رضاه بالموجود، وبه قال مالك والشافعي وأحمد. وفي فتاوى قاضي خان: إن الخيار فيما إذا لم يقبض المبيع أو قبض البعض دون البعض، أما إذا قبض الكل فلا خيار له، بل يأخذ بالحصة.
(4) قوله: فالزائد له؛ لأنه باق على ملكه؛ لأن البيع وقع على مقدار معين، وما وقع على مقدار معين لا يتناول غيره.

وإن باع المذروع هكذا أخذ الأقل بكل الثمن أو ترك، والأكثر له بلا خيار للبائع.
(1) قوله: لأن؛ حاصل الاستدلال أن الذراع وصف، والثمن لا ينقسم على الأوصاف، فكان كل الثمن مقابلاً لكل المبيع، إلا أنه ثبت الخيار للمشتري؛ لأنه فاته وصف مرغوب فيه وقع عليه العقد، وما زاد فللمشتري، ولا خيار فيه للبائع؛ لأن الزائد هاهنا وصف، فكان هذا بمنزلة ما إذا باع بشرط أنه معيب، فإذا هو سليم، وقد عرفت مدار الاستدلال كون الذراع وصفاً.
فيرد عليه: إن الذراع عبارة عن طول وعرض، فكما أنه وصف وعرض، كذلك القلة والكثرة، فكيف جعل الدراع الزائد وصفاً دون القفيز، ومن أين حكم في المسألة الأولى بأن الزائد للبائع، وفي هذه المسألة بأن الأكثر للمشتري؟
فأجاب بعضهم: بأن ما يتعيب بالتبعضيض والتنقيص بهما، فالزيادة والنقصان فيه وصف، وما لا يتعيب بهما فالزيادة والنقصان فيه أصل، والثوب يتعيب بالتنقيص، والحنطة لا تتعيب به. وبعضهم: بأن الوصف ما لوجوده تأثير في تقويم غيره، ولعدمه تأثير في نقصان غيره، والأصل ما لا يكون كذلك، فالقدر في المكيلات والموزونات أصل، والدرع في المذروعات وصف. وبعضهم: بأن ما لا ينتقص الباقي لفواته أصل، كما في الحنطة، وما ينتقص الباقي لفواته وصف كما في الثوب. وأجاب الشارح: بأن المراد بالوصف هاهنا هو الأمر الذي إذا قام بالمحل يوجب في ذلك المحل حسناً أو قبحاً كما في الثوب، فإن الدرع مثلاً في الثوب يوجب حسناً.
Book of Sales / Valid Sales
A flock or a cloth, each sheep or each cubit for such-and-such, and likewise every countable item that varies. If one sells a pile claiming it is a hundred measures for a hundred, and it is less or more, the buyer takes the least according to his share, or he cancels the sale, and what is extra is for the seller.
(1) His statement: 'a flock'; with fatha... (Persian explanation) sheep, plural as 'thilal' like 'kithaf' and 'thilal' like 'kitab'. Thus in Muntaha al-Arab, and in al-Qamus: a group of sheep, and many of them, or specifically ewes.
(2) His statement: 'and likewise'; i.e., and likewise the sale is void in all in the sale of every countable item that varies; because it is not possible to refer to all due to ignorance of the sold item and the price, nor to one because it varies, so it leads to dispute contrary to the first, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is valid in all. The dispute is when he does not specify the total price nor the total of the flock; if he specifies the total price and the total of the flock, or specifies the total of the flock and does not specify the total price, it is valid by agreement. Thus mentioned by al-Birjandi quoting from al-Mujtaba.
(3) His statement: 'the buyer takes the least according to his share'; if he wishes because the measure is a part, and the measure is divisible into parts, or he cancels if he wishes because when the expenditure is divided upon him, his satisfaction with what exists is not complete, and this is the view of Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad. And in Fatawa Qadi Khan: the option is when he has not taken possession of the goods or has taken possession of some and not others; but if he has taken possession of all, then he has no option, rather he takes by the share.
(4) His statement: 'so the excess is for the seller'; because it remains in his ownership; because the sale was for a specific amount, and what is for a specific amount does not include other than it.

And if one sells cloth measured by cubits in this manner, the buyer takes the least for the entire price or leaves it, and the extra is for the buyer without any option for the seller.
(1) His statement: 'because'; the gist of the evidence is that the cubit is a description, and the price is not divided over descriptions, so the entire price corresponds to the entire goods, except that the option is established for the buyer because he missed a desired description that was the subject of the contract, and what is extra is for the buyer, and there is no option for the seller in it because the extra here is a description, so this is like the case where one sells on the condition that it is defective, and it turns out to be sound, and you have known that the basis of the evidence is that the cubit is a description.
It is objected: that the cubit is an expression of length and width, and just as it is a description and a width, so are the fewness and manyness, so how did you make the extra cubit a description without the measure, and how did you rule in the first case that the excess is for the seller, and in this case that the extra is for the buyer?
So some answered: that what is damaged by division and reduction in them, the increase and decrease in it is a description, and what is not damaged by them, the increase and decrease in it is an essence; the garment is damaged by reduction, and wheat is not damaged by it. And some: that the description is that whose existence has an effect on the valuation of other things, and whose non-existence has an effect on the deficiency of others, and the essence is not like that; so quantity in things measured by measure and weight is an essence, and the cubit in things measured by cubits is a description. And some: that what the remainder does not decrease due to its loss is an essence, as in wheat, and what the remainder decreases due to its loss is a description, as in the garment. And the commentator answered: that what is meant by description here is the attribute that when it occurs in a subject causes in that subject goodness or ugliness, as in the garment, for the cubit, for example, in the garment causes goodness.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from a commentary on al-Wiqayah deals with the rulings on sales where the unit of sale is variable. The matn states that selling a flock of sheep or a cloth by the unit (per sheep or per cubit) is problematic because the items are not identical, leading to uncertainty. The commentary explains that such a sale is void (fasid) according to Abu Hanifa because the sale cannot be referred to a single unit due to variation, but the two disciples (Sahibayn) hold it valid when the total price and total quantity are specified. For the pile sale (claimed amount vs actual), the buyer has an option: take the actual amount for its share of the price or cancel. The excess is for the seller. This is agreed upon by Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, but Qadi Khan adds that if the buyer has taken possession of all, he loses the option. For cloth sold by the cubit, if the cloth is longer than stated, the buyer takes the extra without the seller having an option, because the cubit is considered a description (wasf) that affects value, not the essence (asl) of the cloth. The passage then defends this distinction with several arguments: a description is that which, if missing, diminishes the value of the remainder (like cloth) whereas essence is that which does not (like wheat). The commentator concludes that the cubit in cloth is a description because it causes beauty or ugliness.

Key Terms
ثلة (thilla): A flock of sheep, specifically ewes or a mixed flock.
معدود متفاوت (ma'dūd mutafāwit): Countable items that are not uniform (varying in quality or quantity).
صبرة (ṣubra): A pile of grain or similar commodity sold as a whole.
ذراع (dhirā'): A cubit, a unit of length used for measuring cloth.
وصف (waṣf): A separable attribute that enhances or diminishes the value of a thing when present or absent.
أصل (aṣl): The essence or substance of a thing; that which is not affected by increase or decrease in value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When selling a pile of grain claimed to be 100 measures for 100 dirhams, if it turns out to be 80 measures, what can the buyer do according to the majority of scholars (including Abu Hanifa)?
A) Take 80 measures for 80 dirhams
B) Take 80 measures for 100 dirhams
C) Only cancel the sale
D) Demand an additional 20 measures from the seller

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, uncertainty in the unit of sale is resolved by specifying totals, and the classification of the unit as description or essence determines the allocation of surplus.

Deficiency or Excess in Cloth Sale: Description vs Essence
Explains ruling when sold cloth length differs from specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deficiency or excess in cloth sale and explain why length in cloth is a description (wasf) not part of the essence (asl).

Core Idea
In cloth sale, length is a description: deficiency gives buyer choice, excess is buyer's bonus.

Imagine you order a specific length of cloth but receive something shorter – or longer. What are your rights as a buyer? This passage from the Hanafi tradition clarifies that when length is a description affecting usability, the buyer gets an option to accept at full price or reject, and any excess is a free bonus. Understanding the distinction between description (wasf) and essence (asl) is crucial to avoid confusion with other commodities like grain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is being sold? Cloth by the cubit. What is the ruling when length differs? The buyer takes the lesser at full price or leaves; extra is buyer's with no seller option.
This is the core ruling stated at the beginning.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author argues that the cubit is a description (wasf), not part of the essence (asl). The price is not divided over descriptions; the full price covers the entire item.
The proof is a rational analogy (qiyas) based on the nature of descriptions in contracts.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof support the ruling? Since length is a description, any deficiency means the buyer missed a desired attribute, so he has an option. Any excess is an extra description that benefits the buyer.
This contrasts with grain, where quantity is part of the essence and deficiency leads to price reduction.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
An objection is raised: why is length in cloth treated differently from quantity in grain? Several Hanafi responses are given, all centering on impairment: cloth is impaired by reduction, grain is not.
The commentator emphasizes that description affects beauty or ugliness; a nine-cubit cloth may not suffice for a garment.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position is that length in cloth is a description. The buyer thus has the option to take at full price or reject; excess belongs to buyer.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
